  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/901219749" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/901219749?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-library-catalogue">my-library-catalogue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901219749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17218551757555897691">This review has been a long time coming, as Emperor’s Blades is still one of the best books I’ve read this year (actual Goodreads update: “5/5 stars! And a new addition to my small shelf of favorites!”). But for some reason I’ve been stalling on writing the review. Maybe because I know logically the book had a few problems and won’t work for everyone, but I tell you, <b>every single aspect of the story worked for me</b>. So I’m going to proceed fangirling as if I was unaware of of the things others fou</span>
  <span id="freeText17218551757555897691" style="display:none">This review has been a long time coming, as Emperor’s Blades is still one of the best books I’ve read this year (actual Goodreads update: “5/5 stars! And a new addition to my small shelf of favorites!”). But for some reason I’ve been stalling on writing the review. Maybe because I know logically the book had a few problems and won’t work for everyone, but I tell you, <b>every single aspect of the story worked for me</b>. So I’m going to proceed fangirling as if I was unaware of of the things others found fault in. ;P<br><br>To start it off, y’all know how much I love books that have training sequences and competition, and Emperor’s Blades had both in abundance! These Kettral warriors train endlessly in a really brutal regiment to become deadly strike force… and I ate up every single moment. What’s more, the giant birds (badass mofos (cover image background) that for all intents and purposes are feathered dragons), were the cherry on top of what was an already riveting segment. I found this POV (Valyn) the most compelling through the series, made even better by all the great side characters around him.<br><br>And then we move into another POV (Kaden) who is going through training for a religious order and brings with him a whole host of skill-honing (more along the lines of mind-over-body and minor magic-wielding). While Valyn’s POV was fast paced action and excitement, Kaden’s provided a slow burn to break it up. Both were equally interesting to me at this point in the series (this is the problem I get into with waiting too long to review – reading the rest of the series inevitably affects my overall impressions).<br><br>And then we have the final POV, Adare. I really liked the political intrigue this perspective offered, and spent most of the book fascinated with this character. I sincerely couldn’t figure out if she was <i>that</i> painfully nieve, or if there was a grander plan in place I’d yet to discover (you’ll have to tell me what you think – I won’t spoil anything here). What I saw in this first book was the potential for some really great character growth with Adare, and that prospect enticed me.<br><br>This book also contained a mini murder mystery that had me actively trying to narrow down “whodunnit.” I absolutely love when a book gets me analyzing things about it when I’m not actively reading it, so you can see why Emperor’s Blades was such a success for me. I’m just going to try my hardest to forget that someone spilled the beans on whodunnit before I got that far… I’m not bitter.<br><br>Overall, Emperor’s Blades had all of the things that excite me about reading fantasy – in abundance! I won’t endorse it as the perfect read, but it was a perfect match for me and I loved every single gut-wrenching moment.<br><br>Series status: I’ve since finished the entire series and enjoyed it as a whole. The last two are perhaps not quite as good as this first book, but they’re still very much worth reading (mere 4/5 stars ;P). I’ll definitely be picking up anything else Brian Staveley chooses to write.<br><br><b>Recommendations:</b> if you glance at that cover and are even mildly interested in what you see – give the book a go! It’s a well-done trilogy that offers lots of action and excitement. I would feel comfortable handing this to both seasoned fantasy readers and those new to the genre. A great pick! :)<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com</a> <br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27838712.The_Grey_Bastards__The_Lot_Lands___1_" title="The Grey Bastards (The Lot Lands, #1) by Jonathan French" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1447657324s/27838712.jpg" alt="The Grey Bastards (The Lot Lands, #1) by Jonathan French" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15790883.Promise_of_Blood__Powder_Mage___1_" title="Promise of Blood (Powder Mage, #1) by Brian McClellan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1350337505s/15790883.jpg" alt="Promise of Blood (Powder Mage, #1) by Brian McClellan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18947303.Traitor_s_Blade__Greatcoats___1_" title="Traitor's Blade (Greatcoats, #1) by Sebastien de Castell" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1389310293s/18947303.jpg" alt="Traitor's Blade (Greatcoats, #1) by Sebastien de Castell" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27209459.The_Waking_Fire__The_Draconis_Memoria___1_" title="The Waking Fire (The Draconis Memoria, #1) by Anthony Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1458578327s/27209459.jpg" alt="The Waking Fire (The Draconis Memoria, #1) by Anthony Ryan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1307959785s/10790290.jpg" alt="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_2164586382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164586382" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164586382?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=adult-fantasy-sci-fi">adult-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164586382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16662724347394121590">3.75⭐️<br/><br/>This is one of those books that I really liked but find it difficult to review. I’ve very mixed feelings so bear with me here. I'd also like to add that this is after all the first book in the series and when have I ever been blown away by first books, save for some few exceptions here and there? Can’t win ‘em all now, can we?<br/>Don’t get me wrong, I loved it and I found the world and magic system to be especially thrilling and fascinating that invite reader investment but that's not to say i</span>
  <span id="freeText16662724347394121590" style="display:none">3.75⭐️<br /><br />This is one of those books that I really liked but find it difficult to review. I’ve very mixed feelings so bear with me here. I'd also like to add that this is after all the first book in the series and when have I ever been blown away by first books, save for some few exceptions here and there? Can’t win ‘em all now, can we?<br />Don’t get me wrong, I loved it and I found the world and magic system to be especially thrilling and fascinating that invite reader investment but that's not to say it wasn’t without its problems. <br /><br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br /><br />The book kicks off with the emperor assassinated and his heirs, Kaden, Valyn and their sister Adare are all scattered across the globe, each set upon a path by their father. <br /><b>Valyn</b> is on a remote island training to become a Kettral, the Empire’s special/elite forces. <br />Imperial heir, <b>Kaden</b> is cloistered in a mountain abbey, training in the secrets of mental discipline to clear the mind and protect from attack, and seeking to understand the world from a different perspective. <br />And only the eldest daughter, <b>Adare</b> who is suited to rule in all forms but her gender is the only one in Annur, having assumed the role of Minister of Finance. Although she cannot claim the throne, she intently seeks the murderer of her father.<br /><br />I think what I really loved most was the characters and their utter practicality rather than the plot, at least, in the first half of the book. They're royal children who spent their lives taking orders and raised to understand that being a royal comes with a lot of burden, expectations and complications. <br /><br /><br /><b>Expectation vs. reality:</b><br /><br />So, here's what I expected: An epic struggle for the throne (after all, the narrative starts out with the death of the emperor, so, you do the math), some sibling rivalry of sorts, a heavy dose of court and political intrigue and a boatload of conspiracies &amp; plot twists surrounding the mystery behind the death of the emperor.<br />Here's what I actually got: A kind of, coming of age story of the siblings - each going through their own struggles and inner conflicts as they try to deal and come to terms with their new reality.<br />The fact that they are related didn’t really play much of a part until the last few pages, and even then it felt somewhat contrived and forced. <br /><br /><br /><b>plot:</b><br /><br />All in all, the overarching plot was (or had the potential to be) a brilliant one – separate the three leads but have them be intrinsically linked and in danger, in a world that’s both intriguing and interesting, with mythology and mystery. Sounds great right? Well yes, except for the issues that played a big part in hindering me from fully enjoying the story.<br />And though I genuinely liked all three of the protagonists, I had a problem with each and every one of their perspective storylines.<br /><br /><br /><b>Issue #1:</b><br /><br />For starters, Adare was given only a fraction of the page time that her brothers received and I would’ve loved to have seen more of her, particularly given the fact that among the three points of view, her story arc is arguably the one that holds the entire story together and is the most significant in relation to the coming of epic confrontation.<br />It is also through her story that we get a greater sense of the world in which they inhabit, and where we discover that the plot that took down her and her brother's father was much greater and far more complicated. So, I fail to see the reason behind the decision in only giving her (the most important protagonist) less page time than, say, the one whose POV contributes nothing to the story until the very end (more on that below). <br /><br /> - The other problem I had with her was that she’s supposed to be highly trained in the intricacies of politics but not much of it was evident in here and there were lots of inconsistencies in her actions. Her capability was often impeached by committing impetuous and, occasionally, stupid acts for, I'm presuming, no other reason than furthering Staveley’s plot.<br /><br /><b>Issue #2:</b><br /><br />For the first three quarters of the book, Kaden’s storyline contributed little to nothing to the overarching plot and was simply unnecessary. Him getting tested on series of metal endurances by the elder monks or him simply running around with his buddy and getting beat up took up the bulk of his page time until that is, the very last few chapters when things finally started to get… wild. <br /><br /><b>Issue #3:</b><br /><br />Out of the three, it was, of course, Valyn’s storyline that I was continuously captivated by. <b>However,</b> not so fast there, because, his arc too isn’t without its problems. <br />Given his background and the length of time he’d spent training in the elite forces, I expected so much more competency from him. Furthermore, for someone who's also supposed to have been training for years as a team leader, there was not firmness nor toughness in him and his abilities in making executive decisions and leading a team or understanding teamwork, for that matter, left a lot to be desired. I still loved him despite his shortcomings and he was my favourite of the three. <br /><br /><br />That being said, I will definitely continue on with the series and something tells me book #2 will knock my socks right off. <br />It may not sound like I enjoyed it but that couldn't be further from the truth. Putting aside the unnecessary storyline, misshapen characters, and mediocre / inconsistent pacing, there's so much promise and a huge potential in this series and I'm very much looking forward to seeing where the story will go next.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗⤗<br /><br /><br />Got a feeling about this one, folks. 😎<br /><br />So, an Empire on a brink of collapse (I think?), treachery &amp; deceit, a conspiracy, and siblings right in the centre. <br /><br />I don’t know about you but to me, that sounds like a recipe for a badass narrative. 🤞 Well... it’s also a recipe for half the fantasy books out there but... we’re not gonna dwell on <i>that</i>. Girl’s tryin’ to make a point here. <br /><br />Also, I’ve been putting it off for far too long until I was in the right state of mind to read it and it’s only fair that I get compensated for my hard-exercised patience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16662724347394121590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1400326220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1400326220" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1400326220?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1400326220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer913343855488293465"><b>THIS IS ABSOLUTELY DEFINITELY ENTIRELY ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ IN ALL MY BORN DAYS.</b> I just...I cannot...I'VE GOT NO WORDS. It was just such a <i>me</i> book. Omg. Just = OMG. It had <i>everything</i>: maximum stabbiness, torture, bleeding, complex plot, treachery, plot twists, everything I love being murdered, epic stabby royal siblings, psychopaths, assassins, and EVEN A BIT OF SASS NOW AND THEN. <br/><br/>Honestly this is the kind of book I aspire to write.<br/><br/>EXCUSE ME WHILE I LOSE MY MIND IN LOVE AND ADORA</span>
  <span id="freeText913343855488293465" style="display:none"><b>THIS IS ABSOLUTELY DEFINITELY ENTIRELY ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ IN ALL MY BORN DAYS.</b> I just...I cannot...I'VE GOT NO WORDS. It was just such a <i>me</i> book. Omg. Just = OMG. It had <i>everything</i>: maximum stabbiness, torture, bleeding, complex plot, treachery, plot twists, everything I love being murdered, epic stabby royal siblings, psychopaths, assassins, and EVEN A BIT OF SASS NOW AND THEN. <br /><br />Honestly this is the kind of book I aspire to write.<br /><br />EXCUSE ME WHILE I LOSE MY MIND IN LOVE AND ADORATION FOR THIS MASTERPIECE OMG.<br /><br />(Yes, oh shush, I'll review sensibly in a second. Just let me have this wild rabid moment.)<br /><br /><b>NOTE: I listened to the audiobook!</b> Best audiobook ever. Although I listened to it on 2x the speed because who has time for slow voices? Not me. And everything is better in fast-forward (except cake, mate, I like that to last). But the narrator put in a few accents and was just amazing at telling and had an incredible melodic speaking style. So. #win<br /><br /><b>What I particularly loved was how it's a story about three royal siblings.</b> It's actually narrated by all three, although <b>Adare</b> (the only girl) has about 1 chapter to the others' like...10 chapters. HMMMM. But she also had the least interesting storyline so I suppose I'll forgive it. #BenevolentMe But I love love looooved <b>Valyn and Kaden</b> SO VERY MUCH. I can't actually figure out what their ages are?? I think Kaden said he was 17, which I then suppose Valyn was 16? IDEK. LET ME KNOW IF YOU DO KNOW. But Kaden is being trained as a monk at the monstary for his position as Emperor (he's the heir) and Valyn is becoming a Super Awesome Assassin. So like their story lines don't intersect until the end -- BUT IT WAS FREAKISHLY AWESOME WHEN THEY DID. <b>And I just have a huge weakness for brotherly stories.</b> Yayyy the brothers. (I'm actually suffocating I love this so much omg help me.)<br /><br />Plus Valyn was downright AWESOME. He is my favourite. He was badass, but he also failed a lot. He made mistakes, but he also owned them. He is a bundle of stabby rage. BLESS HIS DARK HEART. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And at the end he went TOTALLY dark side when he cut apart that guy and...yeah, I probably shouldn't be so happy when my babies go dark side. BUT THERE YOU GO. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>There's only like 2% romance.</b> Which is like <i>amazing</i>. I'm really tired of books where there's unnecessary romance flung everywhere, BUT THIS WAS PERFECT.<br /><br /><b>Also someone needs to tell the author to chill with the whole "kill your darlings" thing.</b> Granted, he didn't always kill them. He just HURT THEM MAXIMUM AMOUNT. The things these characters went through?!? Particularly Valyn?!? LIKE HOLY KELP. IT WAS INTENSE AND BRUTAL. <b>THe book is everything brutal and gritty.</b> Valyn's assassin/soldier training is insane, and Kaden gets beaten around the monastery super bad in the attempt to teach him how to clear his mind (for a purpose but I won't share because #spoilers). <br /><br />Did I want to kidnap them once or twice to save them? Yes. Did I enjoy that the book knew no chill? Yes.<br /><br /><b>The plot was also majestic.</b> Mostly because it had a bit of a mystery aspect. There were a ton of loose plot threads that didn't seem to connect at all (like random murders, and royalty assassination attempts, and collapsing buildings) and then -- they DID and it was most glorious. <b>The book was constantly exciting and engaging.</b> It packed a ton in and I never wanted to na. In fact, I read this in like a week. Which is absurd and insane for an audibook because I usually take a month. <b>IT WAS SO SO ADDICTIVE, OKAY?!?!</b><br /><br /><b>SMALL LIST OF OTHER THINGS I LOVED:</b><br />• the fact my feels got smashed<br />• magic<br />• evil that does not sleep<br />• giant birds that you can fly on like Gandalf's eagles<br />• royal children fighting for their lives<br />• super gritty battle training<br />• a super sassy assassin<br />• female characters who absolutely KICKED ASS AND TOOK NAMES AND WERE GENERALLY EPIC<br />• intelligent and clever characters<br />• stabbtastic stabbage at all times<br />• misfit bands of warriors who don't like taking orders<br /><br /><b>Although a quiet word about the female characters...</b> Okay, adult epic fantasy is basically always sexist. (In my experience, which is limited so far, I admit.) Even if the women characters are written complex and awesome, they're constantly put in sexist words. Because apparently we can have eagles the size of elephants but we can't have a society not built on a patriarchy. OKAY THEN. <b>But at least this book really promoted the epicness of the women!!</b><br /><br /><b>And I wanted to cry. LIKE A LOT.</b> Because it liked to stab at everything I loved. So nice, so kind, thanks for nothing. BUT DON'T LET THIS FOOL YOU: THIS IS EXACTLY WHAT I WANT IN A BOOK. I <i>want</i> to never believe my favourites are safe. I <i>want</i> to be in a constant state of desperation to find out what happens next. <b>The book is insufferably well written.</b><br /><br /><b>To summarise: I FREAKING LOVED IT.</b> (In case you couldn't tell?!) I loved the characters so so much, because they were complex, dynamic, and amazing. It had a HUGE cast and yet everyone seemed so dimensional. And it effortlessly mixed in dark evil on the horizon, and assassination plots, and gritty and dark princeling training. It was equal parts exciting and heartbreaking. IT SMASHED ME. I'VE NOT FELT THIS ADDICTED TO A BOOK IN A LONG TIME.</span>

<div id="review_781888137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/781888137" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/781888137?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer781888137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2648760752056138131"><b>Sale Alert 19May19 Kindle Deal <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Emperors-Blades-Chronicle-Unhewn-Throne-ebook/dp/B00FCQQCX6/ref=sr_1_39?qid=1558271186&s=digital-text&sr=1-39' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a></b><br/><br/><b>Reread January 2015</b> Dropped 1 star from 5 to 4 <br/><br/>Last year was a big fantasy year for me and my well of experience is bigger now. I still enjoyed this book, it well written with an engaging story, but not quite as much the second time through and <b>I blame my love for Brandon Sanderson's high fantasy</b> for this. There is also Patrick Rothfuss and Joe Abercrombie to blame a little but mostly Sanderson. <br/><br/>See I found Sanderson, Rothfuss and Abercrombie books not long af</span>
  <span id="freeText2648760752056138131" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert 19May19 Kindle Deal <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Emperors-Blades-Chronicle-Unhewn-Throne-ebook/dp/B00FCQQCX6/ref=sr_1_39?qid=1558271186&amp;s=digital-text&amp;sr=1-39" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a></b><br /><br /><b>Reread January 2015</b> Dropped 1 star from 5 to 4 <br /><br />Last year was a big fantasy year for me and my well of experience is bigger now. I still enjoyed this book, it well written with an engaging story, but not quite as much the second time through and <b>I blame my love for Brandon Sanderson's high fantasy</b> for this. There is also Patrick Rothfuss and Joe Abercrombie to blame a little but mostly Sanderson. <br /><br />See I found Sanderson, Rothfuss and Abercrombie books not long after reading The Emperor's Blades this year and they have made my fantasy well much deeper and I expect a little more. The problem I have is with the twist/big reveal toward the end. It is still a good twist I didn't see it coming and was really surprised....but that is part of the problem. The great thing about a Sanderson book is that when the twist happens <i>and it always happens</i> I can look back and see the clues leading to it. I can see how he was the magician who presented me droppings to lead me to one train of thought and then POW hit me with something else entirely. I have grown to love that bait and switch and that is what makes a good twist a Great twist. There isn't quite that subtle layer in the Emperor's Blade. There is the big reveal but even on the reread there really aren't any clues that I should have seen. It all still makes a lot of sense and I really liked it but it didn't have that extra umph at the very end.<br /><br />This was Stavely's debut novel so I'm really excited to see what he follows up with and how much he has grown as a writer. <br /><br /><b>Original review January 2014</b><br /><br />It is the hardest thing to write a review for a book you absolutely love. There is no way that I can get across how marveled by this story I am. The Emperor’s Blades is probably the best new High Fantasy book of the year. Okay so it’s only January but I’m just going to say that the bar has been set <b>extremely</b> high and I unless George RR Martin’s <i>Winds of Winter the 6th book of the A Song of Ice and Fire</i> makes it out this year (highly unlikely) then Brian Staveley’s debut novel might hold this spot in my head and heart all year. I couldn’t believe that this is a debut novel, I’m floored by the depth of the story and this is just the beginning. Brian Staveley will, in all probability, just improve as time goes on and I can’t wait to read anything else he writes.<br /><br />Told from the perspective of the Emperor’s three children Kaden, Valyn and Adare so many different facets of the world were shown to the reader. Instead of telling us that Valyn is a remarkable soldier, like many other fantasy authors do, we are shown the hell of the Kettral training and fully believe after reading those pages that Valyn is a strong warrior. The same goes for Kaden, sent to a monastery for training to become Emperor. His trials are extremely difficult and he is not a pampered prince, I believed that through the years spent there he was able to accomplish the training he needed to be Emperor. <br /><br />There are plots a foot against the empire and all three children of the Emperor, while facing different challenges, play an equally important role in the story. There are ancient enemies from the past, epic battles, trials and tribulations and each one has tempered each of the Emperor’s children into a honed blade against the enemies that are trying to take over the Empire and who murdered the Emperor. Every important facet of the world is explored and fleshed out. There was almost always something of importance happening.<br /><br />There is some set up to this world and so I would say the first 20% runs a little slower than the rest of the story but after that between mysteries and events unfolding I couldn’t tear myself away from the story. No character is safe, there are surprises around every corner, some I guessed most I did not. The author gives plenty of leads, but then the result of the lead was often different and more complex than I originally thought. <br /><br />The intricacy of the story is up there with Tolkien and George RR Martin weaving multiple story lines and plots into a larger grander scheme, but with a prose that is natural, beautiful and easy to read. Every part of the story seemed necessary all of the characters real. Not one character was perfect but all flawed and human. Staveley has created a unique world and really brought it to life in the pages of this story. The only thing I can even complain about is the fact that I started this before the next book was out, I wanted to jump into the next book right away.<br /><br />As a female lover of fantasy the other thing I really liked about The Emperor’s Blades is how many <b>strong female characters</b> there are. Even though the majority of the book is told from Kaden and Valyn’s perspectives some of the strongest characters were female. They made difficult decisions and just because a woman was a warrior didn’t mean she couldn’t have emotions and complexity. He allowed his female characters to be strong without making them into a bitch, they come across as independent, not needing to be saved by a man or anyone else. I appreciate the intricacy that Mr. Staveley put into every one of them.<br /><br />Brian Staveley has a new fan in me. If you only read one Fantasy book this year, this should be it. I look forward to reading it again before the next in the series comes out.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Jan 18,2014 </b><br />Brain Stavelley has set the bar high for this series. The way everything in the story blended together, the reveals I didn't see coming (and there were some slap me in the face doozies), the feelings the book envoked, the intricate world created will be hard to match or beat.<br /><br />I think Mr. Stevelley has the potential to be just as renowned has Tolkien or George R.R. Martin Full review to come...</span>

<div id="review_713308002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713308002" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713308002?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=review-freebie">review-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713308002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer472654428384446432">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2015/12/10/the-emperors-blades/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a>.<br/><br/>After reading fantasy for most of my life, I’ve seen more than a few <i>
  <b>“Next Big Thing”</b>
</i> come along. Some of those hyped novels and series have lived up to the tile, but more than a few have crumbled under the expectations. At least, in my eyes they did. And so when I kept seeing people rave about Brian Staveley’s <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i>, I was a bit skeptical, fearing another letdown if I let myself get sucked into the frenzy. Well, after finally breaking down a</span>
  <span id="freeText472654428384446432" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2015/12/10/the-emperors-blades/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a>.<br /><br />After reading fantasy for most of my life, I’ve seen more than a few <i>
  <b>“Next Big Thing”</b>
</i> come along. Some of those hyped novels and series have lived up to the tile, but more than a few have crumbled under the expectations. At least, in my eyes they did. And so when I kept seeing people rave about Brian Staveley’s <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i>, I was a bit skeptical, fearing another letdown if I let myself get sucked into the frenzy. Well, after finally breaking down and reading it, I now realize all that waiting and doubting was a huge mistake, because this is the real deal in epic fantasy; the Next Big Thing in the genre; the series I can see myself eagerly following for years to come!<br /><br /><i>The Emperor’s Blades</i> follows along behind three of the Emperor’s children: Kaden (the heir), Valyn (the soldier), and Adare (the politician). Each chapters shining the spotlight on one or the other in turn, highlighting their unique struggles, as they are on the edge of maturity yet still trapped in their childhood roles. Sure, there is a bit of resentment of their duties and future roles as their father’s heirs, but their stories are definitely not young adult angst-fests or full-fledged “coming-of-age” tales, but rather a situation where the protagonists just happen to be young adults.<br /><br />As the heir, one would expect Kaden’s story to be centered on court life and political machinations, but Mr. Staveley sidesteps that tired narrative device – instead placing the future Emperor in a monastery on the fringes of civilization. His thoughts and concerns more on news from the outside world and not being beaten by his master for yet another failure in his monastic training than royal ambitions.<br /><br />Valyn, on the other hand, leads an exciting life as a “special forces”-type warrior. His training and the infighting of his fellow cadets turns ugly early and often, as he attempts to become one of the most feared soldiers in the world. If there is truly a “coming-of-age” narrative in the book, I’d point at Valyn’s chapters, because there is a love interest, tough choices, and some emotional turmoil from an unexpected lose; all of which means Valyn displays more angst than his siblings.<br /><br />The final “Blade” in this trio is Adare. This tough, intelligent young woman is knee-deep in political turmoil. As the only child of the Emperor still in the capital, she is quickly engulfed by an upheaval in the government, using her position as a member of the royal cabinet to not only weather the storm but dish out her own punishment to those who have done her wrong. This embroils her in an ugly and very compelling showdown with a powerful religious leader and an alliance with a seemingly friendly politician.<br /><br />All in all, every one of these siblings is a likable, strong, intelligent, and interesting character; each well-rounded, complex and fully capable of carrying their part of the story. Valyn definitely gets more page time, followed closely by Kaden, but even Adare, in her limited appearances, is very interesting, making a reader long for more time to spend tagging along behind her. So, while many times multiple points of view are distracting in an epic fantasy or have interesting and uninteresting parts, all three of these hold their own, making the story a pleasure to read from beginning to end.<br /><br />Naturally, the other character in any epic fantasy is the world building, and Brian Staveley unveils a vibrant, living, and breathing fantasy wonderland in this book. Asian-tinged with sizable dollops of magic, the Annurain world is slowly revealed through the organic teachings of the older characters in the narrative, not through massive info dumps or long “Council of Elrond” like dialogue. And while the depth and breadth of the history and lore are substantial and the magic palpable, Mr. Staveley does a wonderful job of keeping it all just beyond reach, hinting at even more amazing things waiting right around the corner, promising to let you in on the next big secret if you merely stay the course and follow along behind these three characters, who are themselves slowly untangling the mysteries which you yourself long to know.<br /><br />As for the villains, they are numerous and unexpected. No all powerful and completely obvious Sauron-like caricatures here. Nope, each of our young stars deal with their own very different enemies. Whether that be arrogant fellow cadets for Valyn or mysterious creatures for Kaden or powerful high priests for Adare, Mr. Staveley crafts each one differently, shading them in unique ways, so that our Blades are never confronted with the same situation as their sibling a few chapters before. And when the conclusion to the novel finally rolls around, the unveiling of exactly who and what the real villains are and what they are doing might just surprise you.<br /><br />Like I said, this is a book I really fell in love with. Once I became engrossed in the story, I could not stop reading. The characters, the world, the grittiness, and the fast-paced plots held my attention, causing me to stop looking at the clock as I desperately mined this narrative for the answers to all the questions my mind kept creating. Nope, I didn’t get on this bandwagon at the beginning, but now I intend to ride it as far as Mr. Staveley will take me, because <i>Chronicle of the Unhewn Throne</i> is the Next Big Thing out there in my opinion, one which has room for a few more fans if you’d like to jump on next to me and take a fantastic ride.<br /><br />I received this book for free from Tor Books in return for a fair and unbiased review. The thoughts you have read are mine alone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="472654428384446432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_784037850" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/784037850" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1788674-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432902126p2/1788674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/784037850?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/1788674-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1788674-jill?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1788674-jill?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer784037850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11809509992534779308">Here is a (not really) spoiler summary for the first 75% of <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i>: An emperor, dead; a plot to kill his three children, underway; breakneck action to match those high-stakes…completely missing. <br/><br/>We start the book with the death of an emperor—as auspicious a premise as there ever was—but until the final quarter, nothing of importance happens. It’s quite shocking actually: a book that is going to be <i>published</i> could stand to lose its first 300 pages. All that happens in those 300 page</span>
  <span id="freeText11809509992534779308" style="display:none">Here is a (not really) spoiler summary for the first 75% of <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i>: An emperor, dead; a plot to kill his three children, underway; breakneck action to match those high-stakes…completely missing. <br /><br />We start the book with the death of an emperor—as auspicious a premise as there ever was—but until the final quarter, nothing of importance happens. It’s quite shocking actually: a book that is going to be <i>published</i> could stand to lose its first 300 pages. All that happens in those 300 pages is an extended montage scene. The two princes—one training to be an elite soldier, the other serving as a monastic acolyte—get into various unimportant scrapes that are described in painstaking detail. (Literally ‘painstaking’: the pain of these unnecessary details is comparable to the pain of impalement by a stake.) Now I can never resist a good montage scene. Upbeat music coupled with characters getting ready to chase their goals is a perfect combination. But after a while I was hoping for, then praying for, then sacrificing cows at a homemade altar for a conflict to maybe kinda sorta sometime soon appear. Please Zeus?<br /><br />As I waited very patiently, I was subjected to simplistic and forced dialogue that merely served to push the plot along. I also had to suffer dumb characters. Get ready to scoff and eyeroll when a character neglects to notice a big fat whopping clue slapping him on the side of his face! It happens quite a lot, especially with soldier prince. It’s even worse because the story is so emotionally simplistic, it is impossible to connect with the characters. <br /><br />But what bothered me most about this novel was its treatment of female characters. Now this rant does not entirely belong to <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i>. Rather it is the result of hundreds of fantasy books, normally written by male authors, committing the same error. There are three POV characters in this novel, but I’ve only mentioned the two princes. That’s because the princess’s chapters are very few. What’s worse, in each of her chapters we are constantly reminded that this girl cannot be emperor, that she has no role in this man’s fantasy world. I don’t like “strong” female characters who are constantly told that they’re a rarity, that sexism does not want them where they currently have fought to be. Because honestly this just reinforces the idea that it is <i>unnatural</i> for women to be in positions of power. It suggests, quite unconsciously but regardless, that ambitious and successful women are an aberration. Give me a fantasy novel where men and women are equal and <i>absolutely nothing has to be said about it because it’s normal</i>! <br /><br />Despite all these gripes, <i>The Emperor’s Blades</i> is a mildly entertaining novel that will be appreciated by those who like their fantasy more popcorny and less meaty. Do know that this is a series beginner and there is absolutely zero resolution here. Will I be back for book two? Possibly, since the mythology of this world seems interesting and I didn’t learn enough about it for my taste (instead I was treated to another knife fight or something). But I’m going to read reviews carefully before coming back for more to make sure that all of the significant action isn’t stuffed into the final 100 pages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11809509992534779308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1975360495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975360495" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1975360495?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1975360495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16755025015951048346"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Obedience is a knife that cuts the cord of bondage.<br/>Silence is a hammer that shatters the walls of speech.<br/>Stillness is strength; pain a soft bed.<br/>Put down your basin; emptiness is the only vessel.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Four Stars: ✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br/><br/>This book, shockingly, was actually better than I was expecting it to be, just from the blurbs and little snippets I've seen on Goodreads and Audible. I was expecting more or less just another typical modern fantasy book - that wasn't especially interesting or original; b</span>
  <span id="freeText16755025015951048346" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Obedience is a knife that cuts the cord of bondage.<br />Silence is a hammer that shatters the walls of speech.<br />Stillness is strength; pain a soft bed.<br />Put down your basin; emptiness is the only vessel.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Four Stars: ✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br /><br />This book, shockingly, was actually better than I was expecting it to be, just from the blurbs and little snippets I've seen on Goodreads and Audible. I was expecting more or less just another typical modern fantasy book - that wasn't especially interesting or original; but this book surprised me with it's highly original world building and story. It's one of those books that I found myself really enjoying, in spite of the fact that I had a few issues. <br /><br />I have a complaint that I'm going to voice right at the beginning though:<br /><br /><b>The prologue for this book was <i>too good.</i></b><br /><br />I'm serious. It really was WAY too good. Everything about the prologue in this book appealed to me. It carried a sense of weight and reality. The writing was compelling and mysterious. And it introduced a conflict that seemed so new and original and cool. <b>I was thoroughly convinced of this book's merit by the time I got to the end of the prologue.</b><br /><br />And then I got to chapter one, and never heard <i>anything</i> about the contents of the prologue until I was more than halfway through the book. The majority of the book had absolutely nothing to do with the conflict that the prologue introduces. By the time I got to the end of the book I started to understand why the author did this, but it was still frustrating, because <b>I got all excited about a story I would never actually get to read.</b><br /><br />It took me a little while to get into it because of that, but once this book got going, it was really quite good. <br /><br />The worldbuilding and story, in particular, I found to be especially unique. The author took concepts that we are all relatively familiar with and used them in a way that added a unique spin onto these familiar ideas. It's light on the magic content, and this was both a good and a bad thing. Good, because I don't think that the story required a lot of magic content to keep it interesting. Bad, because the magic that *is* in the book I felt could have been better explained, especially regarding the people they call "Leaches". <br /><br />The story is told from the perspective of three siblings - Kaden, Valyn, and Adare. <br /><br /><b>It was the characters that kept me from giving this more than four stars</b>. I found them all to be more than a little bland, and just not very interesting. It felt like they all lacked any real personality, and especially after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27411345.Wrath__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___4_" title="Wrath (The Faithful and the Fallen, #4) by John Gwynne" rel="nofollow noopener">Wrath</a> and The Faithful and the Fallen, I had a really hard time relating to any of the characters in this book. Valyn was BY FAR the most interesting character in the book, but even his character didn't really draw me in until more than halfway through the book. Kaden's *story* kept me interested, but there was literally nothing interesting about him as a person. Neither of them were bad characters, I just really wasn't personally drawn to them.<br /><br />And then there was Adare, who was about as <b>painfully, annoyingly stupid</b> as any character you could read about. She didn't get a lot of airtime in this book, and thank God for that, because I don't think I could have handled more of her than I got.<br /><br />However, in spite of that, <b>the overarching story in the book was seriously excellent</b>, and it's the story and plot of this book that I think sets it apart from other fantasy series in the market today. It felt <b>fresh</b>. We're presented with totally original ideas, combined with familiar elements, that gave this book a really new feeling. So much of today's fantasy feels recycled, but Stavely really did something unique with the story in this book, and I'll definitely be finishing this series because of that.<br /><br />Overall, if you're looking for something different, I really recommend checking this series out. Keep in mind that you might not fall in love with the characters, but if you can get into the story that's being told, it will be well worth your time. <br /><br />Happy reading =]. <br /><br /><i>For this review and more, check out my blog</i>: <a href="https://thoughtsofathousandlives.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Thoughts of a Thousand Lives</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16755025015951048346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_865974862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/865974862" />
    <a title="Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24364577-monica"><img alt="Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394594885p2/24364577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/865974862?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica" href="/user/show/24364577-monica">Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865974862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4296209002760799462">I have read a lot of mediocre reviews on this book. In fact, many of the review sites that I respect the most posited that this book was highly overrated, and they had no idea why Tor had pushed the book so hard. So, I went into this book thinking that it would be an enjoyable read, but nothing too special. Perhaps because of this bias it took me a few chapters to get into the rhythm of the novel, but once I did I was blown away. This is a wonderful debut novel and the start to a new series that</span>
  <span id="freeText4296209002760799462" style="display:none">I have read a lot of mediocre reviews on this book. In fact, many of the review sites that I respect the most posited that this book was highly overrated, and they had no idea why Tor had pushed the book so hard. So, I went into this book thinking that it would be an enjoyable read, but nothing too special. Perhaps because of this bias it took me a few chapters to get into the rhythm of the novel, but once I did I was blown away. This is a wonderful debut novel and the start to a new series that I am sure I will read over and over again.<br /><br /> Once I became engrossed in this book, I found it almost impossible to put down. I love the characters, I love the world, and I love the fast paced and exciting plot. This is one of those novels that I have a hard time finding anything to criticize. If you are a fan of speculative fiction, this book should be on your MUST read now list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4296209002760799462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779904368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2370550119134513375">6 January 2016: <a href='http://amzn.to/1j5SocE' rel='nofollow noopener'>$4.99 on Kindle</a><br/><br/>17 November 2015: $4.99 on Kindle<br/>25 September 2014: $2.99 on Kindle - What a fantastic deal!! Highly, highly recommended.<br/><br/>1/6/2014 Edit: This book comes out next week (I'm ridiculously excited to get my hardcover of it) and I read this interesting blog by Brian Staveley about the inspiration for the Kettral training scenes <a href='http://torforgeblog.com/2014/01/06/giant-hawks-and-mountain-bikes-alternative-training/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a><br/><br/><blockquote>There’s a scene near the middle of The Emperor’s Blades in which a class of Kettral cadets, ultra-elite warriors who fly massive hawks into b</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2370550119134513375" style="display:none">6 January 2016: <a href="http://amzn.to/1j5SocE" rel="nofollow noopener">$4.99 on Kindle</a><br><br>17 November 2015: $4.99 on Kindle<br>25 September 2014: $2.99 on Kindle - What a fantastic deal!! Highly, highly recommended.<br><br>1/6/2014 Edit: This book comes out next week (I'm ridiculously excited to get my hardcover of it) and I read this interesting blog by Brian Staveley about the inspiration for the Kettral training scenes <a href="http://torforgeblog.com/2014/01/06/giant-hawks-and-mountain-bikes-alternative-training/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br><br><blockquote>There’s a scene near the middle of The Emperor’s Blades in which a class of Kettral cadets, ultra-elite warriors who fly massive hawks into battle, are undergoing their final test: Hull’s Trial. People who have read the book ask about this scene a lot, and about Kettral training more generally. They want to know if I’ve served in the military – I haven’t – and then they want to know where in the hell all the training material comes from. The answer (aside from lots and lots of reading about military training) is adventure racing.</blockquote><br><br>12/24/2013 Edit:<br><br>I've just found the map of Annur on Brian Staveley's website! I was hoping to have one of these. Click on the map for a bigger picture<br><br><a href="http://bstaveley.files.wordpress.com/2013/12/emperorsblades_map.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387906189i/7696508._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>Review: <br>Best fantasy book I've read in a long time, quite possibly <i>ever</i>.<br><br><br>I requested this book without even reading the book-blurb because a friend (Thank You <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774374622" rel="nofollow noopener">Cory!!</a>) told me, while still in the middle of reading it, that it was the best fantasy book she'd read in a long time. Fantasy is my home in genre novels, I come back to it time and time again because it's comfortable, exciting, interesting, detailed and emotional. So I started <i>The Emperor's Blades</i> with incredibly high expectations and excitement.<br><br>I was absolutely and thoroughly Blown.Away. This book is amazing. I highlighted dozens of moments throughout this book, was on the edge of my seat for most of it, and was absolutely enthralled the entire journey.<br><br>The intricate, sweeping story that follows the Malkeenian royal line - two brothers and a sister maneuvering between, around and through plots to take the Unhewn Throne from them - is full of intrigue and twists, danger and valor, despair and determination. I can't even do this justice, but I will say it's only the second book to surprise me so completely and throw twists at me I didn't even see coming. After I spent a good portion of the book detailing theories in my head, only to be wrong most of the time, the final twist absolutely blew my mind.<br><br>Kaden, Valyn, and Adare are some of my favorite characters - I was utterly and completely on their side from the very first moments we met each of them. Though I admit Valyn, the warrior, is my favorite, I love all three of them. As I was reading I was eager to see them succeed, to beat the insurmountable odds stacked against them, and terrified that they wouldn't. They aren't infalliable. They aren't perfect. They are, however, absolutely loyal, strong, intelligent, and full of determination. Thank goodness, because this war is going to test the depths of their resolve. Additionally, there are more than a few other characters that I'm dying to know more about. Those for, and against, the emperor both.<br><br>I can't end this review without speaking of the writing itself in <i>The Emperor's Blades</i>. I primarily read for characters, then world, then plot. Prose is important, the way the words are strung together can make or break a story, but it's often the last thing I consider when I decide how much I like a story or not. And if the story here hadn't been so utterly fantastic, if the characters hadn't been so completely intriguing, the world so fascinating - then the words that formed it wouldn't have delighted me so much. But Brian Staveley did something amazing here. He weaved words together in beautiful sentences, gorgeous paragraphs, and painted me a picture that I couldn't look away from. As engrossed as I was in the story, as much as I had to know what was going to happen next, I still stopped and had to re-read a section that was so arresting, so gorgeous, that I couldn't go on without appreciating it for a second, or third, time.<br><br>Part of the journey is complete in <i>The Emperor's Blades</i>, but it's clear there's a lot left to be told. And I, for one, couldn't be happier.<br><br>Review also available on <a href="http://touchthenight.blogspot.com/2013/12/review-emperors-blades-by-brian-staveley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> and <a href="http://angelah.booklikes.com/post/723410/the-emperor-s-blades-by-brian-staveley-best-fantasy-book-in-a-loooonnng-time" rel="nofollow noopener">booklikes</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2370550119134513375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156565978?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156565978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8885202034640114720">This was a fairly standard fantasy story. It was decent without being anything special. <br/><br/>The Emperor has just been assassinated and this book follows the story of his three children as they seek to avoid the same fate. All three of the siblings are in different locations. The eldest, Adare, remained at court with her father and learned the ways of government. The youngest sibling, Kaden, is the heir to the throne and is training in a far flung monastery. The middle sibling, Valyn, is training to </span>
  <span id="freeText8885202034640114720" style="display:none">This was a fairly standard fantasy story. It was decent without being anything special. <br /><br />The Emperor has just been assassinated and this book follows the story of his three children as they seek to avoid the same fate. All three of the siblings are in different locations. The eldest, Adare, remained at court with her father and learned the ways of government. The youngest sibling, Kaden, is the heir to the throne and is training in a far flung monastery. The middle sibling, Valyn, is training to be a warrior with the legendary Kettral. All three were likable enough characters. <br /><br />I liked Valyn's story the most. The Kettral training was interesting and the secondary characters were the most developed. Kaden's story was fairly interesting. Mainly because it eventually lead to us learning who was behind the plot to kill the Imperial family. The mythical, and not human, Csestriim. Adare seemed likable enough. We spent the least amount of time with her. She was focused on discovering who assassinated her father. <br /><br />Despite having a few flaws this book recovered from a slow start to become a fun read. The Csestriim were suitably creepy and villainous, and the various hints of magic we glimpsed were pretty cool.<br /><br />Rating: 4 stars. I'm being kind as the ending was quite good.<br /><br />Audio Note: Simon Vance is a competent narrator, but he will never be a favorite of mine. </span>

<div id="review_2372663361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372663361" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372663361?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=almost-great">almost-great</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372663361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16527314591423476626"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“If we figure everyone might be a murderer, we’re less likely to be disappointed.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Look at me, reading <i>and</i> enjoying adult fantasy! This one starts with the death of an Emperor and follows his three children attempt to navigate the dangerous empire form three separate ends of it. And also uncover the plot that killed their father. Overall, this world was a lot of fun, with a <b>complex and interesting magic system.</b> The world-building was gradual so everything made sense, without being too </span>
  <span id="freeText16527314591423476626" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“If we figure everyone might be a murderer, we’re less likely to be disappointed.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Look at me, reading <i>and</i> enjoying adult fantasy! This one starts with the death of an Emperor and follows his three children attempt to navigate the dangerous empire form three separate ends of it. And also uncover the plot that killed their father. Overall, this world was a lot of fun, with a <b>complex and interesting magic system.</b> The world-building was gradual so everything made sense, without being too 'dumbed' down or slow. I <i>loved</i> the way it came together in the end and the plot-twists perfectly.<br /><br />I loved how this contained <b>morally gray characters who actually make tough decisions.</b> This genre is filled with narrators who claim to be hardened and tough...without any evidence. This took the opposite approach—focusing on the likeable, relatable qualities of our narrators, before showing them make some awful, gut-wrenching decisions. <br /><br />At its core, this book is about people pushed to their limits. <b>All three siblings are tested in unique, difficult ways.</b> Kaden is next in line for the throne, but the monks he trains under barely seem to consider that as they try to break his mind and spirit. Valyn trains to become a member of the empire’s elite fighting force, but the intensity of it pits him against his fellow trainees, his friends and himself. Meanwhile, Adare fights to secure a place in a misogynistic government. Narratively, I found all three voices very similar, but their stories incredibly separate and interesting. <br /><br />As much as I enjoyed this story, <b>I didn’t enjoy the abundance of violence against women.</b> Of course, this universe is very violent and it’s not just restricted to the female characters—but only with the female characters did the violence contain overt sexual overtones. Paired with the way the author chose to <b>describe every single female character’s boobs when introducing them</b>...it felt kind of gross. While Adare’s perspective seems to contradict this objectification, she has <i>so few</i> chapters and it felt unbalanced. <br /><br /><b> In Conclusion:</b><br /><br />A smart, gritty story set in an interesting world, filled with it’s well-executed plot-twists. Falls into typical genre pitfalls regarding female characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16527314591423476626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1003937991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003937991" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003937991?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781466828438" href="/book/show/18525099-the-emperor-s-blades">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003937991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15094515416785749181">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Athena</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4162390-lee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lee</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8323869-mpauli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael</a>.<br/><br/>I <b>HATE</b> being the only one that doesn't like a book everyone loves.<br/><br/>But I'm not going to lie: <b>I didn't like this book.</b> In the strict sense of goodreads rating I should have given it 1 single lonely star, I'm giving it that second one because the last 15% of the book was actually pretty good. <br/><br/>So, let's tally what I thought were this book's sins: <br/><br/><b>BOOK SIN #1</b>. So from the blurb we know that<i>"Kaden, the heir to the Unhewn Throne, has spent eight years sequestered</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15094515416785749181" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer" rel="nofollow noopener">Athena</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4162390-lee" rel="nofollow noopener">Lee</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8323869-mpauli" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael</a>.<br><br>I <b>HATE</b> being the only one that doesn't like a book everyone loves.<br><br>But I'm not going to lie: <b>I didn't like this book.</b> In the strict sense of goodreads rating I should have given it 1 single lonely star, I'm giving it that second one because the last 15% of the book was actually pretty good. <br><br>So, let's tally what I thought were this book's sins: <br><br><b>BOOK SIN #1</b>. So from the blurb we know that<i>"Kaden, the heir to the Unhewn Throne, has spent eight years sequestered in a remote mountain monastery, learning the enigmatic discipline of monks devoted to the Blank God."</i><br> <br>We learn that this is really REALLY important for the heir to know, which prompts the interesting question: what happens if Kaden dies? Because you know, accidents do happen. People die all the time. <br><br>Does Valyn suddenly needs to go spend 8 years learning this too? Wouldn't it have been easier to just send <i>both</i> of them to learn the very important thing? <br><br><b>BOOK SIN #2</b> As stated Kaden has been learning stuff for eight years. <br><br>Well... "learning", he's been doing a lot of random crap that are supposed to be important in the end. <br><br><b>Can you say Karate Kid?</b> <i>Wax on, wax off, wax on...</i> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409316037i/10963855._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The problem is, Kaden doesn't seem to have learned ANYTHING AT ALL. For Hull's sake it's been 8 freaking years. Did all the lessons just go in one ear and out the other? The guy acts like an idiot for 85% of the book!<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #3</b> Actually I think stupidity runs in the family. Valyn has been training for the same amount of time with the super awesome black ops elite force. Yet he seems always to be on the verge of dying, doesn't see the OBVIOUS clues around the "mystery" and is a TERRIBLE team leader. <br><br><b>BOOK SIN #4</b> Also, why the training they endure has to be so violent?! I'm not sure about this idea that beating your apprentice bloody is actually going to make him learn better. It definitely didn't work with these two.<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #5</b> The only smart one in the family is the daughter. Hurray! Of course, she only gets like 5 chapters out of the 50 in the book.<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #6</b> The depiction of the other two important female characters in the book is terrible. <br><blockquote>
  <i>"She didn't look like a flint-hearted killer. At first glance, she actually looked more like a farmer's daughter than a soldier"</i>
</blockquote><br>So, exactly what does a soldier woman looks like? <br><br><b>BOOK SIN #7</b> Valyn is being thrown off a ship by his most hated antagonist, and we get this gem: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"the blond youth grinned down at him..."</i>
</blockquote><br>First, I'm tired of the repetitive descriptions. How many times are you going to tell me Yurl is blond? I got it the first 10000 times. <br><br>Second, seriously? <i>"The blond youth grinned down at him"?</i> This is a person Valyn hates! The "blond youth"? More like "The fucking bastard!" Get your fucking adjectives right!<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #8</b> Obvious romance plot going wrong is obvious.<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #9</b> If the Kettral have to fight in groups, wouldn't it have been a good idea to include some group training in all those years? These guys are all a bunch of lone wolfs. Also, for an elite force they seem TERRIBLE at knowing stuff. Shouldn't they be very good at espionage and information?<br><br><b>BOOK SIN #10</b> <b>WHY DIDN'T THIS BOOK DELIVER ON THE AWESOME PROLOGUE!!</b><br><br>To be honest there was one thing I loved from the book. It has awesome curses, swearwords and phrases. :D<br><br>Also, the worlbuilding seems nice, if overly convoluted at times, and the writing is really good. <br><br>Will I read the second one? Maaaaaybe. If someone promises me Adare gets more page time.<br><br>Would I recommend this? Actually yes. Give it a try. Make me feel even more lonely in my lonely dislike. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15094515416785749181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
